    Making the ctest timeout 200 seconds for Debug
    Some of the tests (tests.unit.plugins.booleans.where_operation for
    example) take close to (or more than) 100 seconds to execute in the
    debug build.  We should look into why these tests are so slow, but
    in the meantime, the builds shouldn't fail.  They will continue to
    fail on KNL, where even the Release build of
    tests.unit.plugins.booleans.where_operation takes 40+ seconds.

Author: Steven R. Brandt <sbrandt@cct.lsu.edu>
Date:   Thu Mar 8 15:27:59 2018 -0600

    Stop generating the surrounding block on function definitions.
    
    This change also causes the functions to be compiled when they are defined,
    rather than every time they're used.
    
    A side-effect of the change (which may or may not be good) is that functions
    cannot be redefined (as they can in Python). Eval.py was updated to use unique
    function names.

commit 1680bafa633392bf5b820b40384964a5af259f94
Author: Kevin Huck <khuck@cs.uoregon.edu>
Date:   Wed Feb 14 18:57:08 2018 -0800

    Fixing shared library link on OSX
    Based on the guidance from this thread:
    https://cmake.org/Bug/bug_relationship_graph.php?bug_id=15126&graph=dependency
    I added "SHARED" to the pybind11_add_module() call in python/src/CMakeLists.txt
    because otherwise, the wrong linker flags are used and Clang complains.
    CMake makes a distinction between shared object libraries and modules that
    are loaded with dlopen() calls.
    
    this manifested itself with this error message when linking Phylanx:
    clang: error: invalid argument '-current_version 0.0.1' only allowed with '-dynamiclib'
    Adding -dynamiclib caused a conflict with -bundle.  Removing -bundle made the
    link work.

commit 3a005626ba53d3f290dabffa5be457f51de19927
Author: Hartmut Kaiser <hartmut.kaiser@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Feb 10 17:44:36 2018 -0600

    Refactoring primitives to reduce compile times and binary sizes
    
    - primitives are not created directly anymore (i.e. using new_<>()), indirectly using
      create_primitive_component() while providing the name of the primitive type to
      create.
    
    This reduces binary sizes by 10-20% and compile and link times by up to 15%

commit 1dc6d7f1f0c04cb9a1117f4caffeedb219eaefb9
Author: Hartmut Kaiser <hartmut.kaiser@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Jan 28 19:04:06 2018 -0600

    Supporting direct positional (symbol) information in PhySL
    
    PhySL now allows for any symbol (identifier or function_call) to encode the line/column information
    of the source code it was generated from: <ident>#line#column. This information is also encoded in the generated
    primitive names: /phylanx/<primitive>#<sequence-nr>[#<instance>]/<compile_id>#<tag1>[#<tag2>], where tag1
    is either the offset as before (if tag2 is missing), otherwise tag1/tag2 encode line/column.
    
    - started to add positional information to PhySL generated from @phyfun decorator
    - added test for facilities related to primitive_name
    - flyby: fixing ast.natvis

commit e67abd1b1893aed90a53fd25e5110bfffab3d5ab

commit e1765e337b254ebafa75a06f7ff61ac8b9ee62bb
Author: Hartmut Kaiser <hartmut.kaiser@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Jan 28 19:04:06 2018 -0600

    Supporting direct positional (symbol) information in PhySL
    
    PhySL now allows for any symbol (identifier or function_call) to encode the line/column information
    of the source code it was generated from: <ident>#line#column. This information is also encoded in the generated
    primitive names: /phylanx/<primitive>#<sequence-nr>[#<instance>]/<compile_id>#<tag1>[#<tag2>], where tag1
    is either the offset as before (if tag2 is missing), otherwise tag1/tag2 encode line/column.
    
    - started to add positional information to PhySL generated from @phyfun decorator
    - added test for facilities related to primitive_name
    - flyby: fixing ast.natvis

commit 06af92a943f68a149181f7b95c857480f4e3076f

commit a33f4147b94f7b54c4b9586e741fbe788851af08
Author: Hartmut Kaiser <hartmut.kaiser@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Jan 11 11:26:03 2018 -0600

    Adding sequence numbers to the names generated for the primitives.
    
    This will enable identifying every primitive instance in an unique way (needed for performance counters).
    The full name of every component is patterned after
    
         /phylanx/<primitive>:<sequence-nr>[:<instance>]/<compile_id>#<tag>
    
    where:
         <primitive>:   the name of primitive type representing the given
                        node in the expression tree
         <sequence-nr>: the sequence number of the corresponding instance
                        of type <primitive>
         <instance>:    (optional), some primitives have additional instance
                        names, for instance references to function arguments
                        have the name of the argument as their <instance>
         <compile_id>:  the sequence number of the invocation of the
                        function phylanx::execution_tree::compile
         <tag>:         the index into the vector of iterators, where the
                        iterator refers to the point of usage of the
                        primitive in the compiled source code

commit 25306d0b3ded48356895d1f90b47373ab15ee4c2
Author: Steven R. Brandt <sbrandt@cct.lsu.edu>

Date:   Mon Dec 4 12:09:49 2017 -0800

    Fixing initialization bug when ELF parsing fails
    When getting command line options from somewhere other than main,
    Linux requires us to parse /proc/self/cmdline because using the
    built in ELF support fails - python is forking the process at some
    point (so GDB tells me) which means that the ELF .init_array
    support doesn't get called.

    Adding support for defining first order functions:
    
        block(
            define(newfunc, arg1, arg2, arg1 + arg2),
            newfunc(41.0, 1.0)
        )
    
    will evaluate to 42 ;)
    
    A `define(x 42)` is equivalent to a variable definition. We might want to remove creating variables implicitly now (on first access).

commit 3c3d7e458358662f3d0047e3b145c81aee3cb1b0
Author: Hartmut Kaiser <hartmut.kaiser@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Sep 17 16:35:04 2017 -0500

    Adding file_read and file_write primitives
    
    - the file_read pattern is 'file_read(_1), where _1 is representing the
      file name to read data from
    - the file_write pattern is 'file_write(_1, _2)', where _1 is the
      representing the file name to write the data to that is represented
      by _2
    
    - both facilities operate on serialized ir::node_data<double> byte streams
    
    - adding corresponding tests
    - introduced literal values in AST (bool, double, uint64, string)
    - this changes construction API for primitives, those now expect to take two
      arguments: a vector of literal values and a vector of other primitives
    - updated add_primitive to be able to handle literal values in addition
      to other primitives
    
    - flyby: adding literal_value test
